<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Tourism</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Travel for recreational or leisure purposes</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Tourism_(disambiguation)" title="Tourism (disambiguation)">Tourism (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Tourist" redirects here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Tourist_(disambiguation)" title="Tourist (disambiguation)">Tourist (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1_times_square_night_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4912" data-file-width="7360" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/1_times_square_night_2013.jpg/220px-1_times_square_night_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/1_times_square_night_2013.jpg/330px-1_times_square_night_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/1_times_square_night_2013.jpg/440px-1_times_square_night_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1_times_square_night_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a> is the hub of the <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway theatre</a> <a href="/wiki/Theater_District,_Manhattan" title="Theater District, Manhattan">district</a> and a major cultural venue in <a href="/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan" title="Midtown Manhattan">Midtown Manhattan</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Pedestrian" title="Pedestrian">pedestrian</a> <a href="/wiki/Intersection_(road)" title="Intersection (road)">intersection</a> also have one of the highest annual attendance-rates of any tourist attraction in the world, estimated at 60 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-curbed.com_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-curbed.com-1">[1]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tourist_taking_photographs_and_video_at_archaelogical_site.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="517" data-file-width="558" decoding="async" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Tourist_taking_photographs_and_video_at_archaelogical_site.jpg/220px-Tourist_taking_photographs_and_video_at_archaelogical_site.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Tourist_taking_photographs_and_video_at_archaelogical_site.jpg/330px-Tourist_taking_photographs_and_video_at_archaelogical_site.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Tourist_taking_photographs_and_video_at_archaelogical_site.jpg/440px-Tourist_taking_photographs_and_video_at_archaelogical_site.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tourist_taking_photographs_and_video_at_archaelogical_site.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A tourist taking photographs and <a href="/wiki/Video" title="Video">video</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_site" title="Archaeological site">archaeological site</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chich%C3%A9n_Itza" title="Chichén Itza">Chichén Itza</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Urban_backpacking.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2216" data-file-width="1840" decoding="async" height="265" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Urban_backpacking.jpg/220px-Urban_backpacking.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Urban_backpacking.jpg/330px-Urban_backpacking.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Urban_backpacking.jpg/440px-Urban_backpacking.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Urban_backpacking.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Backpacker_tourism" title="Backpacker tourism">Backpacker tourism</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><b>Tourism</b> is <a href="/wiki/Travel" title="Travel">travel</a> for pleasure or business; also the theory and practice of <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Touring_(disambiguation)" title="Touring (disambiguation)">touring</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">business</a> of attracting, accommodating, and entertaining tourists, and the business of operating <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Tour_(disambiguation)" title="Tour (disambiguation)">tours</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup>  The <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_Organization" title="World Tourism Organization">World Tourism Organization</a> defines tourism more generally, in terms which go "beyond the common perception of tourism as being limited to holiday activity only", as people "traveling to and staying in places outside their usual environment for not more than one consecutive year for <a href="/wiki/Leisure" title="Leisure">leisure</a> and not less than 24 hours, business and other purposes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unwto1034_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-unwto1034-3">[3]</a></sup> Tourism can be <a href="/wiki/Domestic_tourism" title="Domestic tourism">domestic</a> (within the traveller's own country) or <a href="/wiki/International_tourism" title="International tourism">international</a>, and international tourism has both incoming and outgoing implications on a country's <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_payments" title="Balance of payments">balance of payments</a>.
</p><p>Tourism numbers declined as a result of a strong economic slowdown (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late-2000s_recession" title="Late-2000s recession">late-2000s recession</a>) between the second half of 2008 and the end of 2009, and in consequence of the outbreak of the 2009 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009_flu_pandemic" title="2009 flu pandemic">H1N1 influenza virus</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barom2009_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barom2009-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTOaugust10_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-WTOaugust10-5">[5]</a></sup> but slowly recovered until the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> put an abrupt end to the growth. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_World_Tourism_Organization" title="United Nations World Tourism Organization">United Nations World Tourism Organization</a> estimated that global international tourist arrivals might decrease by 58% to 78% in 2020, leading to a potential loss of US$0.9–1.2 trillion in <a href="/wiki/International_tourism" title="International tourism">international tourism</a> receipts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>Globally, international tourism receipts (the travel item in <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_payments" title="Balance of payments">balance of payments</a>) grew to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1.03</span> trillion (€740 billion) in 2005, corresponding to an increase in <a href="/wiki/Real_versus_nominal_value_(economics)" title="Real versus nominal value (economics)">real terms</a> of 3.8% from 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pr12027_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-pr12027-7">[7]</a></sup> International tourist arrivals surpassed the milestone of 1 billion tourists globally for the first time in 2012,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barom2012_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barom2012-8">[8]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emerging_markets" title="Emerging markets">emerging source markets</a> such as <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> had significantly increased their spending over the previous decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barom201304_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barom201304-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>Global tourism accounts for <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 8% of global <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenhouse-gas" title="Greenhouse-gas">greenhouse-gas</a> emissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Emissions as well as other <a href="/wiki/Impacts_of_tourism" title="Impacts of tourism">significant environmental and social impacts</a> are not always beneficial to local communities and their economies. For this reason, many tourist development organizations have begun to focus on <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_tourism" title="Sustainable tourism">sustainable tourism</a> in order to mitigate the negative effects caused by the growing impact of tourism. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_World_Tourism_Organization" title="United Nations World Tourism Organization">United Nations World Tourism Organization</a> emphasized these practices by promoting tourism as part of the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a>, through programs like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Year_for_Sustainable_Tourism_for_Development" title="International Year for Sustainable Tourism for Development">International Year for Sustainable Tourism for Development</a> in 2017,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and programs like <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Travel_for_SDGs&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Travel for SDGs (page does not exist)">Tourism for SDGs</a> focusing on how <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_8" title="Sustainable Development Goal 8">SDG 8</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_12" title="Sustainable Development Goal 12">SDG 12</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_14" title="Sustainable Development Goal 14">SDG 14</a> implicate tourism in <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">creating a sustainable economy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#Impacts"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Impacts</span></a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2><p>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English-language" title="English-language">English-language</a> word <i>tourist</i> was used in 1772<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> and <i>tourism</i> in 1811.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> These words derive from the word <i>tour</i>, which comes from Old English <span title="Old English (ca. 450-1100)-language text"><i lang="ang">turian</i></span>, from Old French <span title="Old French (842-ca. 1400)-language text"><i lang="fro">torner</i></span>, from Latin <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">tornare</i></span> - "to turn on a lathe", which is itself from Ancient Greek <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><i lang="grc">tornos</i></span> (<span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><span lang="grc">τόρνος</span></span>) - "lathe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miramare_castle_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2136" data-file-width="3797" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Miramare_castle_01.jpg/220px-Miramare_castle_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Miramare_castle_01.jpg/330px-Miramare_castle_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Miramare_castle_01.jpg/440px-Miramare_castle_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miramare_castle_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of the most important tourist destinations in Northern Italy, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> <a href="/wiki/Miramare_Castle" title="Miramare Castle">Miramare Castle</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Green_Northern_Lights_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Green_Northern_Lights_2.jpg/220px-Green_Northern_Lights_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Green_Northern_Lights_2.jpg/330px-Green_Northern_Lights_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Green_Northern_Lights_2.jpg/440px-Green_Northern_Lights_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Green_Northern_Lights_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of the main tourist attractions of northern <a href="/wiki/Lapland_(Finland)" title="Lapland (Finland)">Lapland</a> involves the opportunity to locate bright <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aurora_Borealis" title="Aurora Borealis">Aurora Borealis</a></i> in the sky.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The picture was taken from <a href="/wiki/Rukatunturi" title="Rukatunturi">Ruka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, in 2011.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_July_2011-16.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2896" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Moscow_July_2011-16.jpg/220px-Moscow_July_2011-16.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Moscow_July_2011-16.jpg/330px-Moscow_July_2011-16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Moscow_July_2011-16.jpg/440px-Moscow_July_2011-16.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_July_2011-16.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">Red Square</a>, one of the most famous squares in the world</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Definitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1936, the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> defined a <i>foreign tourist</i> as "someone traveling abroad for at least twenty-four hours". Its successor, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, amended this definition in 1945, by including a maximum stay of six months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theobald_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-theobald-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1941, Hunziker and Kraft defined tourism as "the sum of the phenomena and relationships arising from the travel and stay of non-residents, insofar as they do not lead to <a href="/wiki/Permanent_residency" title="Permanent residency">permanent residence</a> and are not connected with any earning activity."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1941define_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-1941define-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In 1976, the Tourism Society of England's definition was: "Tourism is the temporary, short-term movement of people to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tourist_destination" title="Tourist destination">destinations</a> outside the places where they normally live and work and their activities during the stay at each destination. It includes movements for all purposes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> In 1981, the International Association of Scientific Experts in Tourism defined tourism in terms of particular activities chosen and undertaken outside the home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1994, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> identified three forms of tourism in its <i>Recommendations on Tourism Statistics</i>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Domestic_tourism" title="Domestic tourism">Domestic tourism</a>, involving residents of the given country traveling only within this country</li>
<li>Inbound tourism,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> involving non-residents traveling in the given country</li>
<li>Outbound tourism, involving residents traveling in another country</li></ul>
<p>Other groupings derived from the above grouping:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-glo_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-glo-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>National tourism, a combination of domestic and outbound tourism</li>
<li>Regional tourism, a combination of domestic and inbound tourism</li>
<li>International tourism, a combination of inbound and outbound tourism</li></ul>
<p>The terms <i>tourism</i> and <i>travel</i> are sometimes used interchangeably. In this context, travel has a similar definition to tourism but implies a more purposeful journey. The terms <i>tourism</i> and <i>tourist</i> are sometimes used pejoratively, to imply a shallow interest in the cultures or locations visited. By contrast, <i>traveller</i> is often used as a sign of distinction. The sociology of tourism has studied the cultural values underpinning these distinctions and their implications for class relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism_products">Tourism products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Tourism products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the World Tourism Organization, a tourism product is:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"a combination of tangible and intangible elements, such as natural, cultural, and man-made resources, attractions, facilities, services and activities around a specific center of interest which represents the core of the destination marketing mix and creates an overall visitor experience including emotional aspects for the potential customers. A tourism product is priced and sold through distribution channels and it has a life-cycle".</p></blockquote>
<p>Tourism product covers a wide variety of services including:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Accommodation services from low-cost <a href="/wiki/Homestay" title="Homestay">homestays</a> to five-star hotels</li>
<li>Hospitality services including food and beverage serving centers</li>
<li>Health care services like massage</li>
<li>All modes of transport, its booking and rental</li>
<li>Travel agencies, guided tours and tourist guides</li>
<li>Cultural services such as religious monuments, museums, and historical places</li>
<li>Shopping</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_tourism">International tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: International tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/International_tourism" title="International tourism">International tourism</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=International_tourism&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Internationaltourism.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Internationaltourism.jpg/220px-Internationaltourism.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Internationaltourism.jpg/330px-Internationaltourism.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Internationaltourism.jpg/440px-Internationaltourism.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Internationaltourism.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>International tourism over time</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:International-tourist-arrivals-by-world-region.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="850" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/International-tourist-arrivals-by-world-region.svg/220px-International-tourist-arrivals-by-world-region.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/International-tourist-arrivals-by-world-region.svg/330px-International-tourist-arrivals-by-world-region.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/International-tourist-arrivals-by-world-region.svg/440px-International-tourist-arrivals-by-world-region.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:International-tourist-arrivals-by-world-region.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>International tourist arrivals per year by region</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/International_tourism" title="International tourism">International tourism</a> is tourism that crosses national borders. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Globalisation" title="Globalisation">Globalisation</a> has made tourism a popular global leisure activity. The <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_Organization" title="World Tourism Organization">World Tourism Organization</a> defines tourists as people "traveling to and staying in places outside their usual environment for not more than one consecutive year for leisure, business and other purposes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) estimates that up to 500,000 people are in flight at any one time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boarding.easyjet.a319.arp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1712" data-file-width="2288" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Boarding.easyjet.a319.arp.jpg/220px-Boarding.easyjet.a319.arp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Boarding.easyjet.a319.arp.jpg/330px-Boarding.easyjet.a319.arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Boarding.easyjet.a319.arp.jpg/440px-Boarding.easyjet.a319.arp.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boarding.easyjet.a319.arp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Modern aviation has made it possible to travel long distances quickly.</div></div></div>
<p>In 2010, international tourism reached <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US$" title="US$">US$</a>919B, growing 6.5% over 2009, corresponding to an increase in <a href="/wiki/Real_versus_nominal_value_(economics)" title="Real versus nominal value (economics)">real terms</a> of 4.7%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> In 2010, there were over 940 million international tourist arrivals worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-International_tourism_WTO2011Highlights_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-International_tourism_WTO2011Highlights-32">[32]</a></sup> By 2016 that number had risen to 1,235 million, producing 1,220  billion USD in destination spending.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The COVID-19 crisis had <a href="/wiki/Impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic_on_tourism" title="Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on tourism">significant negative effects on international tourism</a> significantly slowing the overall increasing trend.
</p>
International tourism has significant <a href="/wiki/Impacts_of_tourism" title="Impacts of tourism">impacts on the environment</a>, exacerbated in part by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_aviation" title="Environmental impact of aviation">problems created by air travel</a> but also by other issues, including wealthy tourists bringing lifestyles that stress local infrastructure, water and trash systems among others.</div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Basis">Basis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Basis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The economic foundations of tourism are essentially the cultural assets, the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_property" title="Cultural property">cultural property</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nature" title="Nature">nature</a> of the travel location. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a> are particularly worth mentioning today because they are real tourism magnets. But even a country's current or former form of government can be decisive for tourism. For example, the fascination of the <a href="/wiki/British_royal_family" title="British royal family">British royal family</a> brings millions of tourists to Great Britain every year and thus the economy is around £550 million a year. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> family can be mentioned in Central Europe. According to estimates, the Habsburg brand should generate tourism sales of 60 million euros per year for Vienna alone. The tourist principle "Habsburg sells" applies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tourism typically requires the tourist to feel engaged in a genuine experience of the location they are visiting. According to Dean MacCannell, tourism requires that the tourist can view the toured area as both authentic and different from their own lived experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 113">: 113 </span></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (November 2021)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> By viewing the "exotic," tourists learn what they themselves are not: that is, they are "un-exotic," or normal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (November 2021)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>According to MacCannell, all modern tourism experiences the "authentic" and "exotic" as "developmentally inferior" to the modern—that is, to the lived experience of the tourist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 114">: 114 </span></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (November 2021)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_r.1922.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="933" data-file-width="1435" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_r.1922.jpg/220px-Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_r.1922.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_r.1922.jpg/330px-Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_r.1922.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_r.1922.jpg/440px-Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_r.1922.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_r.1922.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1922 postcard of tourists in the <a href="/wiki/High_Tatras" title="High Tatras">High Tatras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient">Ancient</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ancient">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Travel_literature" title="Travel literature">Travel literature</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:View_from_Vittoria_Lighthouse.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/View_from_Vittoria_Lighthouse.jpg/220px-View_from_Vittoria_Lighthouse.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/View_from_Vittoria_Lighthouse.jpg/330px-View_from_Vittoria_Lighthouse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/View_from_Vittoria_Lighthouse.jpg/440px-View_from_Vittoria_Lighthouse.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:View_from_Vittoria_Lighthouse.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Barcola" title="Barcola">Barcola</a>, a holiday resort in antiquity as well as in the 19th century with the <a href="/wiki/Miramare_Castle" title="Miramare Castle">Miramare Castle</a> and later</div></div></div>
<p>Travel outside a person's local area for leisure was largely confined to wealthy classes, who at times travelled to distant parts of the world, to see great buildings and works of art, <a href="/wiki/Multilingualism" title="Multilingualism">learn new languages</a>, experience new cultures, enjoy pristine nature and to taste different <a href="/wiki/Cuisine" title="Cuisine">cuisines</a>. As early as <a href="/wiki/Shulgi" title="Shulgi">Shulgi</a>, however, kings praised themselves for protecting roads and building way stations for travellers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Travelling for pleasure can be seen in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> as early on as 1500 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spa" title="Spa">spas</a> and coastal resorts such as <a href="/wiki/Baiae" title="Baiae">Baiae</a> were popular among the rich. The Roman upper class used to spend their free time on land or at sea and travelled to their <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">villa urbana</i></span> or <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">villa maritima</i></span>. Numerous villas were located in <a href="/wiki/Campania" title="Campania">Campania</a>, around <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> and in the northern part of the Adriatic as in <a href="/wiki/Barcola" title="Barcola">Barcola</a> near Trieste. <a href="/wiki/Pausanias_(geographer)" title="Pausanias (geographer)">Pausanias</a> wrote his <i>Description of Greece</i> in the second century AD. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_China" title="Ancient China">ancient China</a>, nobles sometimes made a point of visiting <a href="/wiki/Mount_Tai" title="Mount Tai">Mount Tai</a> and, on occasion, all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Five_Sacred_Mountains" title="Five Sacred Mountains">five Sacred Mountains</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval">Medieval</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Medieval">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>By the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-classical" title="Post-classical">post-classical</a> era, many religions, including <a href="/wiki/Christian_pilgrimage" title="Christian pilgrimage">Christianity</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist_pilgrimage" title="Buddhist pilgrimage">Buddhism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Umrah" title="Umrah">Islam</a> had developed traditions of <a href="/wiki/Pilgrimage" title="Pilgrimage">pilgrimage</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Canterbury_Tales" title="The Canterbury Tales">The Canterbury Tales</a></i> (c. 1390s), which uses a pilgrimage as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Framing_device" title="Framing device">framing device</a>, remains a classic of <a href="/wiki/English_literature" title="English literature">English literature</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Journey_to_the_West" title="Journey to the West">Journey to the West</a></i> (c. 1592), which holds a seminal place in <a href="/wiki/Chinese_literature" title="Chinese literature">Chinese literature</a>, has a Buddhist pilgrimage at the center of its narrative.
</p><p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval_Italy" title="Medieval Italy">medieval Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petrarch" title="Petrarch">Petrarch</a> wrote an allegorical account of his 1336 <a href="/wiki/Ascent_of_Mont_Ventoux" title="Ascent of Mont Ventoux">ascent of Mont Ventoux</a> that praised the act of travelling and criticized <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">frigida incuriositas</i></span> (a 'cold lack of curiosity'); this account is regarded as one of the first known instances of travel being undertaken for its own sake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Burgundy" title="Duke of Burgundy">Burgundian</a> poet <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Michault_Taillevent&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Michault Taillevent (page does not exist)">Michault Taillevent</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michault_Taillevent" title="fr:Michault Taillevent">fr</a>]</span> later composed his own horrified recollections of a 1430 trip through the <a href="/wiki/Jura_Mountains" title="Jura Mountains">Jura Mountains</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%22A_Tour_Guide_to_the_Famous_Places_of_the_Capital%22_from_Akizato_Rito%27s_Miyako_meisho_zue_(1787).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1445" data-file-width="1107" decoding="async" height="287" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/%22A_Tour_Guide_to_the_Famous_Places_of_the_Capital%22_from_Akizato_Rito%27s_Miyako_meisho_zue_%281787%29.jpg/220px-%22A_Tour_Guide_to_the_Famous_Places_of_the_Capital%22_from_Akizato_Rito%27s_Miyako_meisho_zue_%281787%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/%22A_Tour_Guide_to_the_Famous_Places_of_the_Capital%22_from_Akizato_Rito%27s_Miyako_meisho_zue_%281787%29.jpg/330px-%22A_Tour_Guide_to_the_Famous_Places_of_the_Capital%22_from_Akizato_Rito%27s_Miyako_meisho_zue_%281787%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/%22A_Tour_Guide_to_the_Famous_Places_of_the_Capital%22_from_Akizato_Rito%27s_Miyako_meisho_zue_%281787%29.jpg/440px-%22A_Tour_Guide_to_the_Famous_Places_of_the_Capital%22_from_Akizato_Rito%27s_Miyako_meisho_zue_%281787%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%22A_Tour_Guide_to_the_Famous_Places_of_the_Capital%22_from_Akizato_Rito%27s_Miyako_meisho_zue_(1787).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Japanese tourist consulting a tour guide and a guide book from Akizato Ritō's <i>Miyako meisho zue</i> (1787)</div></div></div>
<p>In China, 'travel record literature'<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">遊記文學</span></span>, <span title="Pinyin transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">yóujì wénxué</i></span>)</span> became popular during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Song_Dynasty" title="Song Dynasty">Song Dynasty</a> (960–1279).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hargett_67_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-hargett_67-42">[42]</a></sup> Travel writers such as <a href="/wiki/Fan_Chengda" title="Fan Chengda">Fan Chengda</a> (1126–1193) and <a href="/wiki/Xu_Xiake" title="Xu Xiake">Xu Xiake</a> (1587–1641) incorporated a wealth of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geographical" title="Geographical">geographical</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Topographical" title="Topographical">topographical</a> information into their writing, while the 'daytrip essay' <i><a href="/wiki/Su_Shi#Travel_record_literature" title="Su Shi">Record of Stone Bell Mountain</a></i> by the noted poet and statesman <a href="/wiki/Su_Shi" title="Su Shi">Su Shi</a> (1037–1101) presented a philosophical and moral argument as its central purpose.
<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_Tour">Grand Tour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Grand Tour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Grand_Tour" title="Grand Tour">Grand Tour</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Willem_van_Haecht_W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Vasa.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1384" data-file-width="1080" decoding="async" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Willem_van_Haecht_W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Vasa.JPG/220px-Willem_van_Haecht_W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Vasa.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Willem_van_Haecht_W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Vasa.JPG/330px-Willem_van_Haecht_W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Vasa.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Willem_van_Haecht_W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Vasa.JPG/440px-Willem_van_Haecht_W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Vasa.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Willem_van_Haecht_W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Vasa.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Prince Ladislaus Sigismund of Poland visiting Gallery of <a href="/wiki/Cornelis_van_der_Geest" title="Cornelis van der Geest">Cornelis van der Geest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> in 1624</div></div></div>
<p>Modern tourism can be traced to what was known as the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Tour" title="Grand Tour">Grand Tour</a>, which was a traditional trip around <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> (especially <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>), undertaken by mainly <a href="/wiki/Upper_class" title="Upper class">upper-class</a> European young men of means, mainly from Western and Northern European countries. In 1624, the young Prince of <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_IV_Vasa" title="Władysław IV Vasa">Ladislaus Sigismund Vasa</a>, the eldest son of <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_III_Vasa" title="Sigismund III Vasa">Sigismund III</a>, embarked on a journey across Europe, as was in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norm_(sociology)" title="Norm (sociology)">custom</a> among Polish nobility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wladcy12b_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-wladcy12b-44">[44]</a></sup> He travelled through territories of today's Germany, Belgium, the Netherlands, where he admired the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Breda_(1624)" title="Siege of Breda (1624)">Siege of Breda</a> by Spanish forces, France, Switzerland to Italy, Austria, and the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wladcy12b_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-wladcy12b-44">[44]</a></sup> It was an educational journey<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> and one of the outcomes was introduction of <a href="/wiki/Polish_opera" title="Polish opera">Italian opera</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p><p>The custom flourished from about 1660 until the advent of large-scale <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">rail</a> transit in the 1840s and generally followed a standard <a href="/wiki/Travel_itinerary" title="Travel itinerary">itinerary</a>. It was an educational opportunity and <a href="/wiki/Rite_of_passage" title="Rite of passage">rite of passage</a>. Though primarily associated with the <a href="/wiki/British_nobility" title="British nobility">British nobility</a> and wealthy <a href="/wiki/Landed_gentry" title="Landed gentry">landed gentry</a>, similar trips were made by wealthy young men of <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">Northern European</a> nations on the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">Continent</a>, and from the second half of the 18th century some South American, US, and other overseas youth joined in. The tradition was extended to include more of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_class" title="Middle class">middle class</a> after rail and steamship travel made the journey easier, and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_%26_Son" title="Thomas Cook &amp; Son">Thomas Cook</a> made the "Cook's Tour" a byword.
</p><p>The Grand Tour became a real status symbol for upper-class students in the 18th and 19th centuries. In this period, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Joachim_Winckelmann" title="Johann Joachim Winckelmann">Johann Joachim Winckelmann</a>'s theories about the supremacy of classic culture became very popular and appreciated in the European academic world. Artists, writers, and travellers (such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goethe" title="Goethe">Goethe</a>) affirmed the supremacy of classic art of which Italy, France, and Greece provide excellent examples. For these reasons, the Grand Tour's main destinations were to those centers, where upper-class students could find rare examples of classic art and history.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> recently described the Grand Tour in this way:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Three hundred years ago, wealthy young Englishmen began taking a post-<a href="/wiki/Oxbridge" title="Oxbridge">Oxbridge</a> trek through France and Italy in search of art, culture and the roots of <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western civilization</a>. With nearly unlimited funds, aristocratic connections and months (or years) to roam, they <a href="/wiki/Commission_(art)" title="Commission (art)">commissioned paintings</a>, perfected their language skills and mingled with the upper crust of the Continent.</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite>Gross, Matt., <a class="external text" href="http://frugaltraveler.blogs.nytimes.com/2008/09/05/lesons-from-the-frugal-grand-tour/index.html" rel="nofollow">Lessons From the Frugal Grand Tour</a>." <i>New York Times</i> 5 September 2008.</cite></div></blockquote>
<p>The primary value of the Grand Tour, it was believed, laid in the exposure both to the cultural legacy of <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, and to the aristocratic and fashionably polite society of the European continent.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergence_of_leisure_travel">Emergence of leisure travel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Emergence of leisure travel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carl_Spitzweg_047.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1950" data-file-width="2480" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Carl_Spitzweg_047.jpg/220px-Carl_Spitzweg_047.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Carl_Spitzweg_047.jpg/330px-Carl_Spitzweg_047.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Carl_Spitzweg_047.jpg/440px-Carl_Spitzweg_047.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carl_Spitzweg_047.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Englishman in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Campagna" title="Roman Campagna">Campagna</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Spitzweg" title="Carl Spitzweg">Carl Spitzweg</a> (c. 1845)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:225px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Banja_Slatina_ljeto.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3472" data-file-width="4624" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Banja_Slatina_ljeto.jpg/223px-Banja_Slatina_ljeto.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Banja_Slatina_ljeto.jpg/335px-Banja_Slatina_ljeto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Banja_Slatina_ljeto.jpg/446px-Banja_Slatina_ljeto.jpg 2x" width="223"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Banja_Slatina_ljeto.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Slatina Spa in Slatina, Republic of Srpska, BiH is famous for its characteristics and had attracted tourists since 1870s.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Leisure" title="Leisure">Leisure</a> travel was associated with the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> – the first European country to promote leisure time to the increasing industrial population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-singh_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-singh-47">[47]</a></sup> Initially, this applied to the owners of the machinery of production, the economic oligarchy, factory owners and traders. These comprised the new <a href="/wiki/Middle_class" title="Middle class">middle class</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-singh_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-singh-47">[47]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cox_%26_Kings" title="Cox &amp; Kings">Cox &amp; Kings</a> was the first official travel company to be formed in 1758.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>The British origin of this new industry is reflected in many place names. In <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a>, France, one of the first and best-established holiday resorts on the <a href="/wiki/French_Riviera" title="French Riviera">French Riviera</a>, the long esplanade along the seafront is known to this day as the <i><a href="/wiki/Promenade_des_Anglais" title="Promenade des Anglais">Promenade des Anglais</a></i>; in many other historic resorts in <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a>, old, well-established palace hotels have names like the <i><a href="/wiki/Hotel_Bristol" title="Hotel Bristol">Hotel Bristol</a></i>, <i>Hotel Carlton</i>, or <i>Hotel Majestic</i> – reflecting the dominance of English customers.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thomas_Cook_Building,_Leicester,_panels.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1232" data-file-width="2434" decoding="async" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Thomas_Cook_Building%2C_Leicester%2C_panels.jpg/220px-Thomas_Cook_Building%2C_Leicester%2C_panels.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Thomas_Cook_Building%2C_Leicester%2C_panels.jpg/330px-Thomas_Cook_Building%2C_Leicester%2C_panels.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Thomas_Cook_Building%2C_Leicester%2C_panels.jpg/440px-Thomas_Cook_Building%2C_Leicester%2C_panels.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thomas_Cook_Building,_Leicester,_panels.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Panels from the Thomas Cook Building in Leicester, displaying excursions offered by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook" title="Thomas Cook">Thomas Cook</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leicester_Rail_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1266728.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Leicester_Rail_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1266728.jpg/220px-Leicester_Rail_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1266728.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Leicester_Rail_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1266728.jpg/330px-Leicester_Rail_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1266728.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Leicester_Rail_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1266728.jpg/440px-Leicester_Rail_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1266728.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leicester_Rail_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1266728.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leicester_railway_station" title="Leicester railway station">Leicester railway station</a> – built-in 1894 to replace, largely on the same site, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leicester_Campbell_Street_railway_station" title="Leicester Campbell Street railway station">Campbell Street station</a>, the origin for many of Cook's early tours</div></div></div>
<p>A pioneer of the travel agency business, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook" title="Thomas Cook">Thomas Cook</a>'s idea to offer excursions came to him while waiting for the stagecoach on the London Road at <a href="/wiki/Kibworth" title="Kibworth">Kibworth</a>. With the opening of the extended <a href="/wiki/Midland_Counties_Railway" title="Midland Counties Railway">Midland Counties Railway</a>, he arranged to take a group of 540 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperance_Movement" title="Temperance Movement">temperance campaigners</a> from <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leicester_Campbell_Street_railway_station" title="Leicester Campbell Street railway station">Campbell Street station</a> to a rally in <a href="/wiki/Loughborough" title="Loughborough">Loughborough</a>, eleven miles (18 km) away. On 5 July 1841, Thomas Cook arranged for the rail company to charge one <a href="/wiki/Shilling" title="Shilling">shilling</a> per person; this included rail tickets and food for the journey. Cook was paid a share of the fares charged to the passengers, as the railway tickets, being legal contracts between company and passenger, could not have been issued at his own price.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This was the first privately chartered <a href="/wiki/Excursion_train" title="Excursion train">excursion train</a> to be advertised to the general public; Cook himself acknowledged that there had been previous, unadvertised, private excursion trains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> During the following three summers he planned and conducted outings for temperance societies and <a href="/wiki/Sunday_school" title="Sunday school">Sunday school</a> children. In 1844, the Midland Counties Railway Company agreed to make a permanent arrangement with him, provided he found the passengers. This success led him to start his own business running rail excursions for pleasure, taking a percentage of the railway fares.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1855, he planned his first excursion abroad, when he took a group from Leicester to <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a> to coincide with the <a href="/wiki/Exposition_Universelle_(1855)" title="Exposition Universelle (1855)">Paris Exhibition</a>. The following year he started his "grand circular tours" of Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> During the 1860s he took parties to Switzerland, Italy, Egypt, and the United States. Cook established "inclusive independent travel", whereby the traveller went independently but his agency charged for travel, food, and accommodation for a fixed period over any chosen route. Such was his success that the Scottish railway companies withdrew their support between 1862 and 1863 to try the excursion business for themselves.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Significance_of_tourism"><span class="anchor" id="Tourism_industry"></span>Significance of tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Significance of tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ahlbeck_Strandk%C3%B6rbe_2013.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Ahlbeck_Strandk%C3%B6rbe_2013.JPG/220px-Ahlbeck_Strandk%C3%B6rbe_2013.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Ahlbeck_Strandk%C3%B6rbe_2013.JPG/330px-Ahlbeck_Strandk%C3%B6rbe_2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Ahlbeck_Strandk%C3%B6rbe_2013.JPG/440px-Ahlbeck_Strandk%C3%B6rbe_2013.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ahlbeck_Strandk%C3%B6rbe_2013.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Strandkorb" title="Strandkorb">Strandkorb</a> chairs on <a href="/wiki/Usedom" title="Usedom">Usedom Island</a>, Germany. Not only does the service sector grow because of tourism, but also local <a href="/wiki/Craft" title="Craft">manufacturers</a> (like those producing the strandkorb chairs), <a href="/wiki/Retail" title="Retail">retailers</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Real_estate_development" title="Real estate development">real-estate sector</a> and the general <a href="/wiki/City_marketing" title="City marketing">image of a location</a> can benefit as well.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drawienski_Park_Narodowy_-_ruiny_Wegorni.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1064" data-file-width="1416" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Drawienski_Park_Narodowy_-_ruiny_Wegorni.jpg/220px-Drawienski_Park_Narodowy_-_ruiny_Wegorni.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Drawienski_Park_Narodowy_-_ruiny_Wegorni.jpg/330px-Drawienski_Park_Narodowy_-_ruiny_Wegorni.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Drawienski_Park_Narodowy_-_ruiny_Wegorni.jpg/440px-Drawienski_Park_Narodowy_-_ruiny_Wegorni.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Drawienski_Park_Narodowy_-_ruiny_Wegorni.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Drawa_National_Park" title="Drawa National Park">Drawa National Park</a> in Poland, famous for its <a href="/wiki/Canoe" title="Canoe">canoeing</a> routes</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Durban_beach_front_(1_of_1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Durban_beach_front_%281_of_1%29.jpg/220px-Durban_beach_front_%281_of_1%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Durban_beach_front_%281_of_1%29.jpg/330px-Durban_beach_front_%281_of_1%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Durban_beach_front_%281_of_1%29.jpg/440px-Durban_beach_front_%281_of_1%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Durban_beach_front_(1_of_1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a> is well known for its beachfront and "Golden Mile" promenade.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Local_handicraft,_Etosha_National_Park_(Namibia).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3186" data-file-width="3374" decoding="async" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Local_handicraft%2C_Etosha_National_Park_%28Namibia%29.jpg/220px-Local_handicraft%2C_Etosha_National_Park_%28Namibia%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Local_handicraft%2C_Etosha_National_Park_%28Namibia%29.jpg/330px-Local_handicraft%2C_Etosha_National_Park_%28Namibia%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Local_handicraft%2C_Etosha_National_Park_%28Namibia%29.jpg/440px-Local_handicraft%2C_Etosha_National_Park_%28Namibia%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Local_handicraft,_Etosha_National_Park_(Namibia).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tourist buying <a href="/wiki/Handicraft" title="Handicraft">handicrafts</a> in <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>, an important source of income for some tourist destinations</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>tourism industry</b>, as part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Service_sector" title="Service sector">service sector</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> has become an important source of income for many regions and even for entire countries. The <i>Manila Declaration on World Tourism of 1980</i> recognized its importance as "an activity essential to the life of nations because of its direct effects on the social, cultural, educational, and economic sectors of national societies, and on their international relations."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unwto1034_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-unwto1034-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tourism brings large amounts of income into a local economy in the form of payment for <a href="/wiki/Goods_and_services" title="Goods and services">goods and services</a> needed by tourists, accounting as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> for 30% of the world's <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">trade</a> in services, and, as an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invisible_export" title="Invisible export">invisible export</a>, for 6% of overall <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">exports</a> of goods and services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pr12027_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-pr12027-7">[7]</a></sup> It also generates opportunities for <a href="/wiki/Employment" title="Employment">employment</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">service sector of the economy</a> associated with tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTO2012Highlights_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-WTO2012Highlights-54">[54]</a></sup> It is also claimed that travel broadens the mind.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>The hospitality industries which benefit from tourism include <a href="/wiki/Transport" title="Transport">transportation services</a> (such as <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise ships</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">transits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Train" title="Train">trains</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">taxicabs</a>); <a href="/wiki/Lodging" title="Lodging">lodging</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Hotel" title="Hotel">hotels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hostel" title="Hostel">hostels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homestay" title="Homestay">homestays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Resort" title="Resort">resorts</a> and renting out rooms); and entertainment venues (such as <a href="/wiki/Amusement_park" title="Amusement park">amusement parks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Restaurant" title="Restaurant">restaurants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">casinos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Festival" title="Festival">festivals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">shopping malls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_venue" title="Music venue">music venues</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Theatre" title="Theatre">theatres</a>). This is in addition to goods bought by tourists, including <a href="/wiki/Souvenir" title="Souvenir">souvenirs</a>.
</p><p>On the flip-side, tourism can degrade people<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
and sour relationships between host and guest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>The economic foundations of tourism are essentially the cultural assets, the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_property" title="Cultural property">cultural property</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nature" title="Nature">nature</a> of the travel location. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a> are particularly worth mentioning today because they are real tourism magnets. But even a country's current or former form of government can be decisive for tourism. For example, the fascination of the <a href="/wiki/British_royal_family" title="British royal family">British royal family</a> brings millions of tourists to Great Britain every year and thus the economy around £550 million a year. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> family can be mentioned in Central Europe. According to estimates, the Habsburg brand should generate tourism sales of 60 million euros per year for Vienna alone. The tourist principle "Habsburg sells" applies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Tourism.2C_cultural_heritage_and_UNESCO"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism,_cultural_heritage_and_UNESCO">Tourism, cultural heritage and UNESCO</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tourism, cultural heritage and UNESCO">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blue_Shield_Fact_Finding_Mission_Egypt.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Blue_Shield_Fact_Finding_Mission_Egypt.jpg/220px-Blue_Shield_Fact_Finding_Mission_Egypt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Blue_Shield_Fact_Finding_Mission_Egypt.jpg/330px-Blue_Shield_Fact_Finding_Mission_Egypt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Blue_Shield_Fact_Finding_Mission_Egypt.jpg/440px-Blue_Shield_Fact_Finding_Mission_Egypt.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blue_Shield_Fact_Finding_Mission_Egypt.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Blue Shield Fact Finding Mission in Egypt</div></div></div>
<p>Cultural and natural heritage are in many cases the absolute basis for worldwide tourism. Cultural tourism is one of the megatrends that is reflected in massive numbers of overnight stays and sales. As <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> is increasingly observing, the cultural heritage is needed for tourism, but also endangered by it. The "ICOMOS - International Cultural Tourism Charter" from 1999 is already dealing with all of these problems. As a result of the tourist hazard, for example, the <a href="/wiki/Lascaux" title="Lascaux">Lascaux</a> cave was rebuilt for tourists. <a href="/wiki/Overtourism" title="Overtourism">Overtourism</a> is an important buzzword in this area. Furthermore, the focus of UNESCO in war zones is to ensure the protection of cultural heritage in order to maintain this future important economic basis for the local population. And there is intensive cooperation between UNESCO, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_peacekeeping" title="United Nations peacekeeping">United Nations peacekeeping</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blue_Shield_International" title="Blue Shield International">Blue Shield International</a>. There are extensive international and national considerations, studies and programs to protect cultural assets from the effects of tourism and those from war. In particular, it is also about training civilian and military personnel. But the involvement of the locals is particularly important. The founding president of Blue Shield International <a href="/wiki/Karl_von_Habsburg" title="Karl von Habsburg">Karl von Habsburg</a> summed it up with the words: “Without the local community and without the local participants, that would be completely impossible”.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cruise_shipping">Cruise shipping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Cruise shipping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prinzessin_Victoria_Luise_LOC_det.4a15439.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3295" data-file-width="3905" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Prinzessin_Victoria_Luise_LOC_det.4a15439.jpg/170px-Prinzessin_Victoria_Luise_LOC_det.4a15439.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Prinzessin_Victoria_Luise_LOC_det.4a15439.jpg/255px-Prinzessin_Victoria_Luise_LOC_det.4a15439.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Prinzessin_Victoria_Luise_LOC_det.4a15439.jpg/340px-Prinzessin_Victoria_Luise_LOC_det.4a15439.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prinzessin_Victoria_Luise_LOC_det.4a15439.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Prinzessin_Victoria_Luise" title="Prinzessin Victoria Luise">Prinzessin Victoria Luise</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise ship</a> of the world, launched in June 1900 in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> (Germany)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seabourn_Ovation_surrounded_by_palm_trees.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2789" data-file-width="4733" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Seabourn_Ovation_surrounded_by_palm_trees.jpg/220px-Seabourn_Ovation_surrounded_by_palm_trees.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Seabourn_Ovation_surrounded_by_palm_trees.jpg/330px-Seabourn_Ovation_surrounded_by_palm_trees.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Seabourn_Ovation_surrounded_by_palm_trees.jpg/440px-Seabourn_Ovation_surrounded_by_palm_trees.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Seabourn_Ovation_surrounded_by_palm_trees.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The modern cruise ship <i>Seabourn Ovation</i> in the Mediterranean</div></div></div>
<p>Cruising is a popular form of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_tourism" title="Water tourism">water tourism</a>. Leisure <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise ships</a> were introduced by the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peninsular_%26_Oriental_Steam_Navigation_Company" title="Peninsular &amp; Oriental Steam Navigation Company">Peninsular &amp; Oriental Steam Navigation Company</a></i> (P&amp;O) in 1844, sailing from <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">Southampton</a> to destinations such as <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> In 1891, German businessman <a href="/wiki/Albert_Ballin" title="Albert Ballin">Albert Ballin</a> sailed the ship <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Augusta_Victoria_(ship)" title="Augusta Victoria (ship)"><i>Augusta Victoria</i></a> from <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> into the Mediterranean Sea. 29 June 1900 saw the launching of the first purpose-built cruise ship was <i><a href="/wiki/Prinzessin_Victoria_Luise" title="Prinzessin Victoria Luise">Prinzessin Victoria Luise</a></i>, built in Hamburg for the Hamburg America Line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_day_tourism">Modern day tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Modern day tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Many leisure-oriented tourists travel to <a href="/wiki/Seaside_resort" title="Seaside resort">seaside resorts</a> on their nearest coast or further afield. Coastal areas in the tropics are popular in both summer and winter.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_tourism">Mass tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Mass tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Adolf_Friedrich_Erdmann_von_Menzel_044.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1003" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="108" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Adolf_Friedrich_Erdmann_von_Menzel_044.jpg/220px-Adolf_Friedrich_Erdmann_von_Menzel_044.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Adolf_Friedrich_Erdmann_von_Menzel_044.jpg/330px-Adolf_Friedrich_Erdmann_von_Menzel_044.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Adolf_Friedrich_Erdmann_von_Menzel_044.jpg/440px-Adolf_Friedrich_Erdmann_von_Menzel_044.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Adolf_Friedrich_Erdmann_von_Menzel_044.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Reisepläne</i> (<i>Travel plans</i>) by <a href="/wiki/Adolph_Menzel" title="Adolph Menzel">Adolph Menzel</a> (1875)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rom_fountain_of_Trevi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Rom_fountain_of_Trevi.jpg/220px-Rom_fountain_of_Trevi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Rom_fountain_of_Trevi.jpg/330px-Rom_fountain_of_Trevi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Rom_fountain_of_Trevi.jpg/440px-Rom_fountain_of_Trevi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rom_fountain_of_Trevi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mass tourism at the <a href="/wiki/Trevi_Fountain" title="Trevi Fountain">Trevi Fountain</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barceloneta_2007.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Barceloneta_2007.jpg/220px-Barceloneta_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Barceloneta_2007.jpg/330px-Barceloneta_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Barceloneta_2007.jpg/440px-Barceloneta_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Barceloneta_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tourists at the Mediterranean Coast of <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, 2007</div></div></div>
<p>Academics have defined <b>mass tourism</b> as travel by groups on pre-scheduled tours, usually under the organization of tourism professionals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> This form of tourism developed during the second half of the 19th century in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and was pioneered by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook" title="Thomas Cook">Thomas Cook</a>.
