Cook took advantage of Europe's rapidly expanding railway network and established a company that offered affordable <a href="/wiki/Day_trip" title="Day trip">day trip</a> excursions to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commoners" title="Commoners">the masses</a>, in addition to longer holidays to Continental Europe, India, Asia and the Western Hemisphere which attracted wealthier customers. By the 1890s over 20,000 tourists per year used <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_%26_Son" title="Thomas Cook &amp; Son">Thomas Cook &amp; Son</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mass_Tourism_p._74_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mass_Tourism_p._74-68">[68]</a></sup>
</p><p>The relationship between tourism companies, transportation operators and hotels is a central feature of mass tourism. Cook was able to offer prices that were below the publicly advertised price because his company purchased large numbers of tickets from railroads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mass_Tourism_p._74_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mass_Tourism_p._74-68">[68]</a></sup> One contemporary form of mass tourism, <a href="/wiki/Package_tour" title="Package tour">package tourism</a>, still incorporates the partnership between these three groups.
</p><p>Travel developed during the early 20th century and was facilitated by the development of the automobiles and later by airplanes.
Improvements in transport allowed many people to travel quickly to places of leisure interest so that more people could begin to enjoy the benefits of leisure time.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">Continental Europe</a>, early <a href="/wiki/Seaside_resort" title="Seaside resort">seaside resorts</a> included: <a href="/wiki/Heiligendamm" title="Heiligendamm">Heiligendamm</a>, founded in 1793 at the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>, being the first seaside resort; <a href="/wiki/Ostend" title="Ostend">Ostend</a>, popularised by the people of <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>; <a href="/wiki/Boulogne-sur-Mer" title="Boulogne-sur-Mer">Boulogne-sur-Mer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deauville" title="Deauville">Deauville</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Parisians</a>; <a href="/wiki/Taormina" title="Taormina">Taormina</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, the first seaside resorts in the European style were at <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City,_New_Jersey" title="Atlantic City, New Jersey">Atlantic City</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>.
</p><p>By the mid-20th century, the Mediterranean Coast became the principal mass tourism destination. The 1960s and 1970s saw mass tourism play a major role in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_miracle#Mass_tourism_and_emigration" title="Spanish miracle">Spanish economic "miracle"</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.
</p><p>In the 1960s and 1970s, scientists discussed negative socio-cultural impacts of tourism on host communities. Since the 1980s the positive aspects of tourism began to be recognized as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Niche_tourism">Niche tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Niche tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a more comprehensive list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_adjectival_tourisms" title="List of adjectival tourisms">List of adjectival tourisms</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cristo_Rei_(36211699613).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2141" data-file-width="1996" decoding="async" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Cristo_Rei_%2836211699613%29.jpg/220px-Cristo_Rei_%2836211699613%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Cristo_Rei_%2836211699613%29.jpg/330px-Cristo_Rei_%2836211699613%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Cristo_Rei_%2836211699613%29.jpg/440px-Cristo_Rei_%2836211699613%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cristo_Rei_(36211699613).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Christ_the_King_(Almada)" title="Christ the King (Almada)">Sanctuary of Christ the King</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Almada" title="Almada">Almada</a>, has become one of the places most visited for religious tourism.</div></div></div>
<p>Niche tourism refers to the numerous specialty forms of tourism that have emerged over the years, each with its own adjective. Many of these terms have come into common use by the tourism industry and academics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Others are emerging concepts that may or may not gain popular usage. Examples of the more common niche tourism markets are:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Agritourism" title="Agritourism">Agritourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Birth_tourism" title="Birth tourism">Birth tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Culinary_tourism" title="Culinary tourism">Culinary tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cultural_tourism" title="Cultural tourism">Cultural tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dark_tourism" title="Dark tourism">Dark tourism</a> (also called "black tourism" or "grief tourism")</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eco_tourism" title="Eco tourism">Eco tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Extreme_tourism" title="Extreme tourism">Extreme tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Geotourism" title="Geotourism">Geotourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heritage_tourism" title="Heritage tourism">Heritage tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LGBT_tourism" title="LGBT tourism">LGBT tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">Medical tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Film_tourism" title="Film tourism">Film tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nautical_tourism" title="Nautical tourism">Nautical tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pop-culture_tourism" title="Pop-culture tourism">Pop-culture tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Religious_tourism" title="Religious tourism">Religious tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sex_tourism" title="Sex tourism">Sex tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Slum_tourism" title="Slum tourism">Slum tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sports_tourism" title="Sports tourism">Sports tourism</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virtual_tourism" title="Virtual tourism">Virtual tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/War_tourism" title="War tourism">War tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wellness_tourism" title="Wellness tourism">Wellness tourism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wildlife_tourism" title="Wildlife tourism">Wildlife tourism</a></li></ul>
</div>
<p>Other terms used for niche or specialty travel forms include the term "destination" in the descriptions, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Destination_wedding" title="Destination wedding">destination weddings</a>, and terms such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Location_vacation" title="Location vacation">location vacation</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Winter_tourism">Winter tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Winter tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_ski_areas_and_resorts" title="List of ski areas and resorts">List of ski areas and resorts</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winter_sport" title="Winter sport">Winter sport</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hollywood_Wax_Museum_-_Pigeon_Forge,_TN.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="882" data-file-width="1346" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Hollywood_Wax_Museum_-_Pigeon_Forge%2C_TN.jpg/220px-Hollywood_Wax_Museum_-_Pigeon_Forge%2C_TN.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Hollywood_Wax_Museum_-_Pigeon_Forge%2C_TN.jpg/330px-Hollywood_Wax_Museum_-_Pigeon_Forge%2C_TN.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Hollywood_Wax_Museum_-_Pigeon_Forge%2C_TN.jpg/440px-Hollywood_Wax_Museum_-_Pigeon_Forge%2C_TN.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hollywood_Wax_Museum_-_Pigeon_Forge,_TN.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An example of a tourist destination in Pigeon Forge, Tennessee</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arctic_circle_santa_village.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="896" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Arctic_circle_santa_village.jpg/220px-Arctic_circle_santa_village.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Arctic_circle_santa_village.jpg/330px-Arctic_circle_santa_village.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Arctic_circle_santa_village.jpg/440px-Arctic_circle_santa_village.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arctic_circle_santa_village.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Santa_Claus_Village" title="Santa Claus Village">Santa Claus Village</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Circle" title="Arctic Circle">Arctic Circle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rovaniemi" title="Rovaniemi">Rovaniemi</a>, Finland is one of the significant tourist places in the Northern Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/St._Moritz" title="St. Moritz">St. Moritz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> became the cradle of the developing winter tourism in the 1860s: hotel manager Johannes Badrutt invited some summer guests from England to return in the winter to see the snowy landscape, thereby inaugurating a popular trend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> It was, however, only in the 1970s when winter tourism took over the lead from summer tourism in many of the Swiss ski resorts. Even in winter, up to one third of all guests (depending on the location) consist of non-skiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>
</p><p>Major <a href="/wiki/Ski_resort" title="Ski resort">ski resorts</a> are located mostly in the various European countries (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosnia-Herzegovina" title="Bosnia-Herzegovina">Bosnia-Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_ski_areas_and_resorts_in_Europe#Poland" title="List of ski areas and resorts in Europe">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>), <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (e.g. Montana, Utah, Colorado, California, Wyoming, Vermont, New Hampshire, New York) <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_developments">Recent developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Recent developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_Yacht_Harbour_Residence_Rostock_Yachthafenresidenz_Hohe_D%C3%BCne_6.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="622" data-file-width="913" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Aerial_view_Yacht_Harbour_Residence_Rostock_Yachthafenresidenz_Hohe_D%C3%BCne_6.jpg/220px-Aerial_view_Yacht_Harbour_Residence_Rostock_Yachthafenresidenz_Hohe_D%C3%BCne_6.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Aerial_view_Yacht_Harbour_Residence_Rostock_Yachthafenresidenz_Hohe_D%C3%BCne_6.jpg/330px-Aerial_view_Yacht_Harbour_Residence_Rostock_Yachthafenresidenz_Hohe_D%C3%BCne_6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Aerial_view_Yacht_Harbour_Residence_Rostock_Yachthafenresidenz_Hohe_D%C3%BCne_6.jpg/440px-Aerial_view_Yacht_Harbour_Residence_Rostock_Yachthafenresidenz_Hohe_D%C3%BCne_6.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_Yacht_Harbour_Residence_Rostock_Yachthafenresidenz_Hohe_D%C3%BCne_6.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Destination_hotel" title="Destination hotel">destination hotel</a> in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>: <i>Yacht Harbour Residence</i> in <a href="/wiki/Warnem%C3%BCnde" title="Warnemünde">Rostock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mecklenburg" title="Mecklenburg">Mecklenburg</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Can_you_see_the_surfer%3F_(33988985575).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Can_you_see_the_surfer%3F_%2833988985575%29.jpg/220px-Can_you_see_the_surfer%3F_%2833988985575%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Can_you_see_the_surfer%3F_%2833988985575%29.jpg/330px-Can_you_see_the_surfer%3F_%2833988985575%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Can_you_see_the_surfer%3F_%2833988985575%29.jpg/440px-Can_you_see_the_surfer%3F_%2833988985575%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Can_you_see_the_surfer%3F_(33988985575).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nazar%C3%A9,_Portugal" title="Nazaré, Portugal">Nazaré, Portugal</a>, is now listed in the <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a></i> for the biggest waves ever surfed, and has become a worldwide tourist attraction.</div></div></div>
<p>There has been an up-trend in tourism over the last few decades,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="This information is too vague. (November 2013)">vague</span></a></i>]</sup> especially in Europe, where international travel for short breaks is common. Tourists have a wide range of budgets and tastes, and a wide variety of resorts and hotels have developed to cater for them. For example, some people prefer simple beach vacations, while others want more specialized holidays, quieter resorts, family-oriented holidays, or niche market-targeted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Destination_hotel" title="Destination hotel">destination hotels</a>.
</p><p>The developments in <a href="/wiki/Aviation" title="Aviation">air transport</a> infrastructure, such as <a href="/wiki/Wide-body_aircraft" title="Wide-body aircraft">jumbo jets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost airlines</a>, and more <a href="/wiki/Accessible_tourism" title="Accessible tourism">accessible</a> <a href="/wiki/Airport" title="Airport">airports</a> have made many types of tourism more affordable. A major factor in the relatively low cost of air travel is the <a href="/wiki/Aviation_fuel#Tax" title="Aviation fuel">tax exemption for aviation fuels</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WHO" title="WHO">WHO</a> estimated in 2009 that there are around half a million people on board aircraft at any given time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> There have also been changes in lifestyle, for example, some retirement-age people sustain year-round tourism. This is facilitated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electronic_commerce" title="Electronic commerce">internet sales</a> of tourist services. Some sites have now started to offer <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_packaging" title="Dynamic packaging">dynamic packaging</a>, in which an inclusive price is quoted for a tailor-made package requested by the customer upon impulse.
</p><p>There have been a few setbacks in tourism, such as the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorist threats</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tourist_destination" title="Tourist destination">tourist destinations</a>, such as in <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a> and several European cities. Also, on 26 December 2004, a <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a>, caused by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake">2004 Indian Ocean earthquake</a>, hit the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_Asia" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories in Asia">Asian countries</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a>. Thousands of lives were lost including many tourists. This, together with the vast clean-up operations, stopped or severely hampered tourism in the area for a time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p><p>Individual low-price or even zero-price overnight stays have become more popular in the 2000s, especially with a strong growth in the <a href="/wiki/Hostel" title="Hostel">hostel</a> market and services like <a href="/wiki/CouchSurfing" title="CouchSurfing">CouchSurfing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbnb" title="Airbnb">airbnb</a> being established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newyorkercouch_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-newyorkercouch-77">[77]</a></sup> There has also been examples of jurisdictions wherein a significant portion of GDP is being spent on altering the primary sources of revenue towards tourism, as has occurred for instance in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainable_tourism">Sustainable tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sustainable tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_tourism" title="Sustainable tourism">Sustainable tourism</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sustainable_tourism&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_renowned_Kakum_National_Reserve.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/The_renowned_Kakum_National_Reserve.jpg/320px-The_renowned_Kakum_National_Reserve.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/The_renowned_Kakum_National_Reserve.jpg/480px-The_renowned_Kakum_National_Reserve.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/The_renowned_Kakum_National_Reserve.jpg/640px-The_renowned_Kakum_National_Reserve.jpg 2x" width="320"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_renowned_Kakum_National_Reserve.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Canopy Walkway at <a href="/wiki/Kakum_National_Park" title="Kakum National Park">Kakum National Park</a> in Ghana, ensuring that tourists have least direct impact on the surrounding ecology. The visitor park received the Global Tourism for Tomorrow Award the following year.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sustainable_tourism" title="Sustainable tourism">Sustainable tourism</a> is a concept that covers the complete tourism experience, including concern for <a href="/wiki/Impacts_of_tourism" title="Impacts of tourism">economic, social and environmental issues</a> as well as attention to improving tourists' experiences and addressing the needs of host communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Sustainable tourism should embrace concerns for environmental protection, social equity, and the quality of life, cultural diversity, and a dynamic, viable economy delivering jobs and prosperity for all.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> It has its roots in <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a> and there can be some confusion as to what "sustainable tourism" means.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sustainable_tourism_:3_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainable_tourism_:3-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 23">: 23 </span></sup> There is now broad consensus that tourism should be <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainable</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> In fact, all forms of tourism have the potential to be sustainable if planned, developed and managed properly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sustainable_tourism_:3_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainable_tourism_:3-81">[81]</a></sup> Tourist development organizations are promoting sustainable tourism practices in order to mitigate negative effects caused by the growing <a href="/wiki/Impacts_of_tourism" title="Impacts of tourism">impact of tourism</a>, for example its environmental impacts. 
</p>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_World_Tourism_Organization" title="United Nations World Tourism Organization">United Nations World Tourism Organization</a> emphasized these practices by promoting sustainable tourism as part of the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a>, through programs like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Year_for_Sustainable_Tourism_for_Development" title="International Year for Sustainable Tourism for Development">International Year for Sustainable Tourism for Development</a> in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> There is a direct link between sustainable tourism and several of the 17 Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sustainable_tourism_:3_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainable_tourism_:3-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 26">: 26 </span></sup> Tourism for SDGs focuses on how <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_8" title="Sustainable Development Goal 8">SDG 8</a> ("decent work and economic growth"), <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_12" title="Sustainable Development Goal 12">SDG 12</a> ("responsible consumption and production") and <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_14" title="Sustainable Development Goal 14">SDG 14</a> ("life below water") implicate tourism in <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">creating a sustainable economy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Improvements are expected to be gained from suitable management aspects and including sustainable tourism as part of a broader <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a> strategy.</div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecotourism">Ecotourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ecotourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">Ecotourism</a></div>
<p>Ecotourism, also known as ecological tourism, is responsible travel to fragile, pristine, and usually protected areas that strives to be low-impact and (often) small-scale. It helps educate the traveller; provides funds for conservation; directly benefits the economic development and political empowerment of local communities, and fosters respect for different cultures and for human rights. <i>Take only memories and leave only footprints</i> is a very common slogan in protected areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Tourist destinations are shifting to low carbon emissions following the trend of visitors more focused in being environmentally responsible adopting a sustainable behavior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Volunteer_tourism">Volunteer tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Volunteer tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volunteer_tourism" title="Volunteer tourism">Volunteer tourism</a></div>
<p>Volunteer tourism (or voluntourism) is growing as a largely Western phenomenon, with volunteers travelling to aid those less fortunate than themselves in order to counter global inequalities. Wearing (2001) defines volunteer tourism as applying "to those tourists who, for various reasons, volunteer in an organised way to undertake holidays that might involve aiding or alleviating the material poverty of some groups in society".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> VSO was founded in the UK in 1958 and the US Peace Corps was subsequently founded in 1960. These were the first large scale voluntary sending organisations, initially arising to modernise less economically developed countries, which it was hoped would curb the influence of communism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>This form of tourism is largely praised for its more sustainable approach to travel, with tourists attempting to assimilate into local cultures, and avoiding the criticisms of consumptive and exploitative mass tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> However, increasingly, voluntourism is being criticised by scholars who suggest it may have negative effects as it begins to undermine local labour, and force unwilling host communities to adopt Western initiatives,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> while host communities without a strong heritage fail to retain volunteers who become dissatisfied with experiences and volunteer shortages persist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Increasingly, organisations such as VSO have been concerned with community-centric volunteer programmes where power to control the future of the community is in the hands of local people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pro-poor_tourism">Pro-poor tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Pro-poor tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><video class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="523" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Community_Tourism_(Riven_No_2).webm" height="124" id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Community_Tourism_%28Riven_No_2%29.webm/220px--Community_Tourism_%28Riven_No_2%29.webm.jpg" preload="none" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="844520" data-framerate="25" data-height="168" data-shorttitle="WebM source" data-title="Original WebM file, 298 × 168 (845 kbps)" data-width="298" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e0/Community_Tourism_%28Riven_No_2%29.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp8, vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="201952" data-framerate="25" data-height="120" data-shorttitle="VP9 120P" data-title="Lowest bandwidth VP9 (120P)" data-transcodekey="120p.vp9.webm" data-width="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/e0/Community_Tourism_%28Riven_No_2%29.webm/Community_Tourism_%28Riven_No_2%29.webm.120p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/><source data-bandwidth="214584" data-framerate="25" data-height="160" data-shorttitle="WebM 160P" data-title="Low bandwidth WebM (160P)" data-transcodekey="160p.webm" data-width="284" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/e0/Community_Tourism_%28Riven_No_2%29.webm/Community_Tourism_%28Riven_No_2%29.webm.160p.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp8, vorbis"'/></video> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Community_Tourism_(Riven_No_2).webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Community tourism in Sierra Leone <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikibooks.org/wiki/Development_Cooperation_Handbook/Stories/Community_Tourism" title="b:Development Cooperation Handbook/Stories/Community Tourism">→ The story of a community in Sierra Leone trying to manage tourism in a responsible manner</a> <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Film-Camera.png"><img alt="Film-Camera.png" data-file-height="392" data-file-width="646" decoding="async" height="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Film-Camera.png/17px-Film-Camera.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Film-Camera.png/26px-Film-Camera.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Film-Camera.png/34px-Film-Camera.png 2x" width="17"/></a> <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PL32A3F6F949A3F26D" rel="nofollow">Playlist</a></div></div></div>
<p>Pro-poor tourism, which seeks to help the poorest people in developing countries, has been receiving increasing attention by those involved in development; the issue has been addressed through small-scale projects in local communities and through attempts by Ministries of Tourism to attract large numbers of tourists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Research by the <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Development_Institute" title="Overseas Development Institute">Overseas Development Institute</a> suggests that neither is the best way to encourage tourists' money to reach the poorest as only 25% or less (far less in some cases) ever reaches the poor; successful examples of money reaching the poor include mountain-climbing in <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> and cultural tourism in <a href="/wiki/Luang_Prabang" title="Luang Prabang">Luang Prabang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-odi.org.uk_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-odi.org.uk-95">[95]</a></sup> There is also the possibility of pro-poor tourism principles being adopted in centre sites of regeneration in the developed world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recession_tourism">Recession tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Recession tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Recession tourism is a travel trend which evolved by way of the world economic crisis. Recession tourism is defined by low-cost and high-value experiences taking place at once-popular generic retreats. Various recession tourism hotspots have seen business boom during the recession thanks to comparatively low costs of living and a slow world job market suggesting travellers are elongating trips where their money travels further. This concept is not widely used in tourism research. It is related to the short-lived phenomenon that is more widely known as <a href="/wiki/Staycation" title="Staycation">staycation</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_tourism">Medical tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Medical tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">Medical tourism</a></div>
<p>When there is a significant price difference between countries for a given medical procedure, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> where there are different regulatory regimes, in relation to particular medical procedures (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Dentistry" title="Dentistry">dentistry</a>), travelling to take advantage of the price or regulatory differences is often referred to as "medical tourism".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Educational_tourism">Educational tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Educational tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Educational tourism is developed because of the growing popularity of teaching and learning of knowledge and the enhancing of technical competency outside of the classroom environment. Brent W. Ritchie, publisher of Managing Educational Tourism, created a study of a geographic subdivision to demonstrate how tourism educated high school students participating in foreign exchange programs over the last 15 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> In educational tourism, the main focus of the tour or leisure activity includes visiting another country to learn about the culture, study tours, or to work and apply skills learned inside the classroom in a different environment, such as in the International Practicum Training Program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> In 2018, one impact was many exchange students traveled to America to assist students financially in order to maintain their secondary education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Event_tourism">Event tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Event tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This type of tourism is focused on tourists coming into a region to either participate in an event or to see an organized event put on by the city/region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-102">[102]</a></sup> This type of tourism can also fall under <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_tourism" title="Sustainable tourism">sustainable tourism</a> as well and companies that create a <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_event_management" title="Sustainable event management">sustainable event</a> to attend open up a chance to not only the consumer but their workers to learn and develop from the experience. Creating a sustainable atmosphere creates a chance to inform and encourage sustainable practices. An example of event tourism would be the music festival <a href="/wiki/South_by_Southwest" title="South by Southwest">South by Southwest</a> that is hosted in <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin, Texas</a> annually. Every year people from all over the world flock to the city for one week to sit in on technology talks and see bands perform. People are drawn here to experience something that they are not able to experience in their hometown, which defines event tourism.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Creative_tourism">Creative tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Creative tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FF_of_Hartwell_welcomes_Indonesians.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="815" data-file-width="768" decoding="async" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/FF_of_Hartwell_welcomes_Indonesians.jpg/220px-FF_of_Hartwell_welcomes_Indonesians.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/FF_of_Hartwell_welcomes_Indonesians.jpg/330px-FF_of_Hartwell_welcomes_Indonesians.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/FF_of_Hartwell_welcomes_Indonesians.jpg/440px-FF_of_Hartwell_welcomes_Indonesians.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FF_of_Hartwell_welcomes_Indonesians.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Friendship_Force_International" title="Friendship Force International">Friendship Force</a> visitors from Indonesia meeting their hosts in <a href="/wiki/Hartwell,_Georgia" title="Hartwell, Georgia">Hartwell, Georgia</a>, United States</div></div></div>
<p>Creative tourism has existed as a form of <a href="/wiki/Cultural_tourism" title="Cultural tourism">cultural tourism</a>, since the early beginnings of tourism itself. Its European roots date back to the time of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Tour" title="Grand Tour">Grand Tour</a>, which saw the sons of aristocratic families travelling for the purpose of mostly interactive, educational experiences. More recently, creative tourism has been given its own name by Crispin Raymond and Greg Richards,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ct_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-ct-103">[103]</a></sup> who as members of the Association for Tourism and Leisure Education (ATLAS), have directed a number of projects for the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, including cultural and crafts tourism, known as <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_tourism" title="Sustainable tourism">sustainable tourism</a>. They have defined "creative tourism" as tourism related to the active participation of travellers in the <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a> of the host community, through interactive workshops and informal learning experiences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ct_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-ct-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>Meanwhile, the concept of creative tourism has been picked up by high-profile organizations such as <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, who through the <a href="/wiki/Creative_Cities_Network" title="Creative Cities Network">Creative Cities Network</a>, have endorsed creative tourism as an engaged, <a href="/wiki/Authenticity_(reenactment)" title="Authenticity (reenactment)">authentic</a> experience that promotes an active understanding of the specific cultural features of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Location_(geography)" title="Location (geography)">place</a>. UNESCO wrote in one of its documents: "'Creative Tourism' involves more interaction, in which the visitor has an educational, emotional, social, and participative interaction with the place, its living culture, and the people who live there. They feel like a citizen."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Saying so, the tourist will have the opportunity to take part in workshops, classes and activities related to the culture of the destination.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greg_Richards_-_Conferencia_Turismo_Creativo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="320" data-file-width="480" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Greg_Richards_-_Conferencia_Turismo_Creativo.jpg/220px-Greg_Richards_-_Conferencia_Turismo_Creativo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Greg_Richards_-_Conferencia_Turismo_Creativo.jpg/330px-Greg_Richards_-_Conferencia_Turismo_Creativo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Greg_Richards_-_Conferencia_Turismo_Creativo.jpg/440px-Greg_Richards_-_Conferencia_Turismo_Creativo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greg_Richards_-_Conferencia_Turismo_Creativo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A tourism conference underway</div></div></div>
<p>More recently, creative tourism has gained popularity as a form of cultural tourism, drawing on active participation by travellers in the culture of the host communities they visit. Several countries offer examples of this type of tourism development, including the United Kingdom, Austria, France, the Bahamas, Jamaica, Spain, Italy, New Zealand and South Korea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>
</p><p>The growing interest of tourists<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> in this new way to discover a culture regards particularly the operators and branding managers, attentive to the possibility of attracting a quality tourism, highlighting the intangible heritage (craft workshops, cooking classes, etc.) and optimizing the use of existing infrastructure (for example, through the rent of halls and auditoriums).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Experiential_tourism">Experiential tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Experiential tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Experiential_travel" title="Experiential travel">Experiential travel</a> (or "immersion travel") is one of the major market trends in the modern tourism industry. It is an approach to travelling which focuses on experiencing a country, city or particular place by connecting to its <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">history</a>, people, food and <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>The term "experiential travel" has been mentioned in publications since 1985,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> but it was not discovered as a meaningful market trend until much later.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dark_tourism">Dark tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Dark tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dark_tourism" title="Dark tourism">Dark tourism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Poland_-_Czermna_-_Chapel_of_Skulls_-_interior_06.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Poland_-_Czermna_-_Chapel_of_Skulls_-_interior_06.jpg/220px-Poland_-_Czermna_-_Chapel_of_Skulls_-_interior_06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Poland_-_Czermna_-_Chapel_of_Skulls_-_interior_06.jpg/330px-Poland_-_Czermna_-_Chapel_of_Skulls_-_interior_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Poland_-_Czermna_-_Chapel_of_Skulls_-_interior_06.jpg/440px-Poland_-_Czermna_-_Chapel_of_Skulls_-_interior_06.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Poland_-_Czermna_-_Chapel_of_Skulls_-_interior_06.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skull_Chapel,_Czermna" title="Skull Chapel, Czermna">Skull Chapel</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kudowa-Zdr%C3%B3j" title="Kudowa-Zdrój">Kudowa-Zdrój</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lower_Silesian_Voivodeship" title="Lower Silesian Voivodeship">Lower Silesian Voivodeship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, is an example of an attraction for <a href="/wiki/Dark_tourism" title="Dark tourism">dark tourism</a>. Its interior walls, ceiling and foundations are adorned by human remains. It is the only such monument in Poland, and one of six in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>One emerging area of special interest has been identified by Lennon and Foley (2000)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> as <a href="/wiki/Dark_tourism" title="Dark tourism">"dark" tourism</a>. This type of tourism involves visits to "dark" sites, such as battlegrounds, scenes of horrific crimes or acts of <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>, for example <a href="/wiki/Internment" title="Internment">concentration camps</a>. Its origins are rooted in fairgrounds and medieval fairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Philip_Stone" title="Philip Stone">Philip Stone</a> argues that dark tourism is a way of imagining one's own death through the real death of others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Erik_H_Cohen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Erik H Cohen (page does not exist)">Erik H Cohen</a> introduces the term "<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Populo_sites&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Populo sites (page does not exist)">populo sites</a>" to evidence the educational character of dark tourism. Popular sites transmit the story of victimized people to visitors. Based on a study at <a href="/wiki/Yad_Vashem" title="Yad Vashem">Yad Vashem</a>, the Shoah (Holocaust) memorial museum in Jerusalem, a new term—<i>in populo</i>—is proposed to describe dark tourism sites at a spiritual and population center of the people to whom a tragedy befell. Learning about the Shoah in Jerusalem offers an encounter with the subject which is different from visits to sites in Europe, but equally authentic. It is argued that a dichotomy between "authentic" sites at the location of a tragedy and "created" sites elsewhere is insufficient. Participants' evaluations of seminars for European teachers at Yad Vashem indicate that the location is an important aspect of a meaningful encounter with the subject. Implications for other cases of dark tourism at <i>in populo</i> locations are discussed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> In this vein, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Tarlow" title="Peter Tarlow">Peter Tarlow</a> defines dark tourism as the tendency to visit the scenes of tragedies or historically noteworthy deaths, which continue to impact our lives. This issue cannot be understood without the figure of trauma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>Victoria Mitchell et al. suggest that dark tourism seems to be a heterogeneous discipline. There is a great dispersion of definitions, knowledge production and meanings revolving around the term. In fact, dark tourism practices vary in culture and time. Qualitative speaking, dark tourism experience is pretty different from leisure practices. To fill the gap, the existent definitions should be catalogued in sub-categories to form an all-encompassing model that expands the current understanding of dark tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> In consonance with this, M. Apleni et al. argue dark tourism helps the industry not to be fragmented before the ongoing states of crises the activity often faces. They cite the case of terrorism which paves the way for the construction of a new dark site. Dark tourism plays a leading role not only in enhancing destination resilience but also in helping communities to deal with traumatic experiences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_tourism">Social tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Social tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Social tourism is making tourism available to poor people who otherwise could not afford to travel for their education or recreation. It includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Youth_hostels" title="Youth hostels">youth hostels</a> and low-priced holiday accommodation run by church and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voluntary_organisation" title="Voluntary organisation">voluntary organisations</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_unions" title="Trade unions">trade unions</a>, or in Communist times <a href="/wiki/Combine_(enterprise)" title="Combine (enterprise)">publicly owned enterprises</a>. In May 1959, at the second Congress of Social Tourism in Austria, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Hunziker#Social_tourism" title="Walter Hunziker">Walter Hunziker</a> proposed the following definition: "Social tourism is a type of tourism practiced by low-income groups, and which is rendered possible and facilitated by entirely separate and therefore easily recognizable services".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Doom_tourism">Doom tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Doom tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Perito_Moreno_Glacier_Patagonia_Argentina_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1333" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Perito_Moreno_Glacier_Patagonia_Argentina_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.JPG/220px-Perito_Moreno_Glacier_Patagonia_Argentina_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Perito_Moreno_Glacier_Patagonia_Argentina_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.JPG/330px-Perito_Moreno_Glacier_Patagonia_Argentina_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Perito_Moreno_Glacier_Patagonia_Argentina_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.JPG/440px-Perito_Moreno_Glacier_Patagonia_Argentina_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Perito_Moreno_Glacier_Patagonia_Argentina_Luca_Galuzzi_2005.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Perito_Moreno_Glacier" title="Perito Moreno Glacier">Perito Moreno Glacier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a></div></div></div>
<p>Also known as "tourism of doom," or "last chance tourism", this emerging trend involves travelling to places that are environmentally or otherwise threatened (such as the ice caps of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kilimanjaro" title="Mount Kilimanjaro">Mount Kilimanjaro</a>, the melting glaciers of <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a>, or the coral of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Barrier_Reef" title="Great Barrier Reef">Great Barrier Reef</a>) before it is too late. Identified by travel trade magazine <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Travel_Age_West&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Travel Age West (page does not exist)">Travel Age West</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> editor-in-chief Kenneth Shapiro in 2007 and later explored in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> this type of tourism is believed to be on the rise. Some see the trend as related to <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_tourism" title="Sustainable tourism">sustainable tourism</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">ecotourism</a> due to the fact that a number of these tourist destinations are considered threatened by environmental factors such as global warming, overpopulation or climate change. Others worry that travel to many of these threatened locations increases an individual's <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">carbon footprint</a> and only hastens problems threatened locations are already facing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_tourism">Religious tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Religious tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religious_tourism" title="Religious tourism">Religious tourism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade,_Rome,_Italy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2975" data-file-width="4470" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade%2C_Rome%2C_Italy.jpg/220px-Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade%2C_Rome%2C_Italy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade%2C_Rome%2C_Italy.jpg/330px-Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade%2C_Rome%2C_Italy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade%2C_Rome%2C_Italy.jpg/440px-Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade%2C_Rome%2C_Italy.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade,_Rome,_Italy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="St. Peter's Basilica">St. Peter's Basilica</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a>, the papal enclave within the Italian city of Rome, one of the largest religious tourism sites in the world</div></div></div>
<p>Religious tourism, in particular <a href="/wiki/Pilgrimage" title="Pilgrimage">pilgrimage</a>, can serve to strengthen <a href="/wiki/Faith" title="Faith">faith</a> and to demonstrate devotion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Religious tourists may seek destinations whose image encourages them to believe that they can strengthen the religious elements of their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Self-identity" title="Self-identity">self-identity</a> in a positive manner. Given this, the perceived image of a destination may be positively influenced by whether it conforms to the requirements of their religious self-identity or not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="DNA_tourism">DNA tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: DNA tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>DNA tourism, also called "ancestry tourism" or "heritage travel", is tourism based on DNA testing. These tourists visit their remote relatives or places where their ancestors came from, or where their relatives reside, based on the results of DNA tests. DNA testing became a growing trend in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impacts">Impacts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Impacts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Impacts_of_tourism" title="Impacts of tourism">Impacts of tourism</a></div>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Impacts_of_tourism" title="Impacts of tourism">Impacts of tourism</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Impacts_of_tourism&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Impacts_of_tourism.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="364" data-file-width="1366" decoding="async" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Impacts_of_tourism.jpg/300px-Impacts_of_tourism.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Impacts_of_tourism.jpg/450px-Impacts_of_tourism.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Impacts_of_tourism.jpg/600px-Impacts_of_tourism.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Impacts_of_tourism.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Impacts of tourism</div></div></div>
<p>Tourism brings both positive and negative impacts on tourist destinations. The traditionally-described domains of tourism impacts are <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socio-cultural_development" title="Socio-cultural development">socio-cultural</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental" title="Environmental">environmental</a> dimensions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> The economic effects of tourism include improved <a href="/wiki/Tax_revenue" title="Tax revenue">tax revenue</a> and personal income, increased <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">standards of living</a>, and more employment opportunities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Sociocultural impacts are associated with interactions between people with differing cultural backgrounds, attitudes and behaviors, and relationships to material goods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Impacts_of_tourism_Mason_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Impacts_of_tourism_Mason-134">[134]</a></sup> Environmental impacts can have both direct effects including degradation of habitat, vegetation, air quality, bodies of water, the <a href="/wiki/Water_table" title="Water table">water table</a>, wildlife, and changes in natural phenomena, and indirect effects, such as increased harvesting of natural resources to supply food, indirect air and water pollution (including from flights, transport and the manufacture of food and souvenirs for tourists).
</p>
Tourism also brings positive and negative health outcomes for local people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Impacts_of_tourism_:6_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Impacts_of_tourism_:6-135">[135]</a></sup> The short-term negative impacts of tourism on residents' health are related to the density of tourist's arrivals, risk of disease transmission, road accidents, higher crime levels, as well as traffic congestion, crowding, and other stressful factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Impacts_of_tourism_:7_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Impacts_of_tourism_:7-136">[136]</a></sup> In addition, residents can experience anxiety and depression related to their risk perceptions about mortality rates, food insecurity, contact with infected tourists, etc., which can result in negative mental health outcomes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Impacts_of_tourism_:5_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Impacts_of_tourism_:5-137">[137]</a></sup> At the same time, there are positive long-term impacts of tourism on residents’ health and well-being outcomes through improving healthcare access positive emotions, novelty, and social interactions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Impacts_of_tourism_:6_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-Impacts_of_tourism_:6-135">[135]</a></sup></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Growth">Growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_Organization" title="World Tourism Organization">World Tourism Organization</a> (UNWTO) forecasts that international tourism will continue growing at the average annual rate of 4%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-predict_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-predict-138">[138]</a></sup> With the advent of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electronic_commerce" title="Electronic commerce">e-commerce</a>, tourism products have become prominent traded items on the internet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Tourism products and services have been made available through intermediaries, although tourism providers (hotels, airlines, etc.), including small-scale operators, can sell their services directly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> This has put pressure on intermediaries from both on-line and traditional shops.
</p><p>It has been suggested there is a strong correlation between tourism expenditure per capita and the degree to which countries play in the global context.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-correl_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-correl-143">[143]</a></sup> Not only as a result of the important economic contribution of the tourism industry, but also as an indicator of the degree of confidence with which global citizens leverage the resources of the globe for the benefit of their <a href="/wiki/Community-based_economics" title="Community-based economics">local economies</a>. This is why any projections of growth in tourism may serve as an indication of the relative influence that each country will exercise in the future.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:White_Knight_Two_and_SpaceShipTwo_from_directly_below.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2206" data-file-width="3089" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/White_Knight_Two_and_SpaceShipTwo_from_directly_below.jpg/220px-White_Knight_Two_and_SpaceShipTwo_from_directly_below.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/White_Knight_Two_and_SpaceShipTwo_from_directly_below.jpg/330px-White_Knight_Two_and_SpaceShipTwo_from_directly_below.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/White_Knight_Two_and_SpaceShipTwo_from_directly_below.jpg/440px-White_Knight_Two_and_SpaceShipTwo_from_directly_below.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:White_Knight_Two_and_SpaceShipTwo_from_directly_below.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/SpaceShipTwo" title="SpaceShipTwo">SpaceShipTwo</a>, a major project in <a href="/wiki/Space_tourism" title="Space tourism">space tourism</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Space_tourism">Space tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Space tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Space_tourism" title="Space tourism">Space tourism</a></div>
<p>There has been a limited amount of orbital <a href="/wiki/Space_tourism" title="Space tourism">space tourism</a>, with only the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Space_Agency" title="Russian Space Agency">Russian Space Agency</a> providing transport to date. A 2010 report into space tourism anticipated that it could become a billion-dollar market by 2030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_tourism">Sports tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Sports tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_tourism" title="Sports tourism">Sports tourism</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2017</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Since the late 1980s, <a href="/wiki/Sports_tourism" title="Sports tourism">sports tourism</a> has become increasingly popular. Events such as <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cricket_World_Cups&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cricket World Cups (page does not exist)">Cricket World Cups</a> and <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a> have enabled specialist travel companies to gain official ticket allocation and then sell them in packages that include flights, hotels and excursions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism_security">Tourism security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tourism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Tourism security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tourism security is a subdiscipline of tourist studies that explores the factors that affect the ontological security of tourists. Risks are evaluated by their impact and nature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Tourism security includes methodologies, theories and techniques oriented to protect the organic image of tourist destinations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Three academic waves are significant in tourism security: risk perception theory, disaster management, and post-disaster consumption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup>
</p><p>Andrew Spencer &amp; Peter Tarlow argue that tourism security is not an easy concept to define. It includes a set of sub-disciplines, and global risks different in nature which cause different effects in the tourism industry. The rise of tourism security and safety as a consolidated discipline coincides with the globalization and ultimate maturation of the industry worldwide. Some threats include, for example, terrorist groups looking to destabilize governments affecting not only the local economies but killing foreign tourists to cause geopolitical tensions between delivery-country and receiving-tourist countries. Today, island destinations are more affected by terrorism and other global risks than other continent destinations <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup>
</p>
